<Text>Although I had to wait 40 minutes to sit at the bar, it was well worth it. I had the Poke Bowl, which was  the equivalent of deconstructed sushi rolls. Amazing. Tuna, salmon, crab, tobiko,  and seaweed over rice with spicy mayo. Must do again!</Text><gmap_id>0x808fcca239a23525:0xd94b97e3b83d3cbd< /gmap_id><pics>None<//pics>< UserId.>
113004946455307380397</UserId.>
<Resp>None</Resp><rating>5</rating></record>
</dataset><record>
<pictures>None<//pictures>< review>
I came to Blush on a Wednesday afternoon around 4:30 and was immediately greeted by both the server and the manager.  We were seated right away (the place was pretty empty).

Our server was very nice and informative -- she gave us tips on what customized drinks we could make based on our taste preferences.  My favorite was regular vodka, soda water, lemon lime slush with strawberry puree.

We had the following items from the HH menu:

- rose roll - delicious and large portions

- hamachi spoon - very fresh fish, but too much sauce.

- sushi tacos - large portion, but i wish they would make it so that it was easier to split with another person.  because each taco had different toppings, I did not get to try all three flavors.

- cheese fondue - the portion was on the small side.  there's too much bread for the amount of cheese provided.  I wish they had other dippers like vegetables instead of all bread.

- oysters - unfortunately, the oysters were bad.  they didn't taste particularly fresh and they were not cleaned (lots of shells and rocks in every bite).

I highly recommend coming here for happy hour, but do yourself a favor and skip the oysters!</review>

<userid>111401897967097745156</userid><Name>Kimberly Ann Graham<//Name><time>1412564232760< /time><Rating>4<//Rating>< text>
Located in San Jose's new Public Market, Blush Raw Bar is part of an experiment in a new way to dine and socialize.  Tucked in the back corner, Blush has a high end feeling while still in the middle of all the fun of the Markets.  Went there to meet up with friends, have some drinks/apps and watch a Blues singer/band perform.  Starting with cocktails, I ordered the Blush Sangria "Blushie".  It seems to me to be a their take on an Aqui's Swirl (a local favorite) and only moderately successful.  Next were the small plates.  Coconut Tuna Tartare was good, feel like it was a little on the bland side but very fresh.  Carpaccio was good, I liked the presentation and flavor.  The Ahi Club was one of my favorite things, ahi tuna seared perfectly with an asian slaw in middle of parmesan crusted/grilled bread, served with wasabi aioli.  This is the one I'd order again!  The Cheese Fondue would go in the same category with the Ahi Club, yummy!  We ordered a dozen of their fresh oysters, they were very fresh but some of them were noticeabley smaller than the others.  Can't wait to go back and sample a bit more of their menu as well as the Market!<//text>

It was the first time I‚Äôve decided to use a professional service for my taxes. I‚Äôve been doing my taxes via TurboTax for the past 10 years, never without a hiccup.

I decided to go to H&R block for my 2015 returns due to the complicated stock investments from my current employer. I figured, a professional will give me peace of mind. Boy was I wrong. It‚Äôs the exact opposite.

A few weeks ago, I received a letter from the IRS stating that my 2015 taxes were filed Incorrectly and that I now owe $8,885. I was completely shocked and appalled  given the fact that I knew that was the exact year I had Fred Stevens from H&R Block file my taxes.

I called back Fred Stevens with complete urgency. It took him a few days to call me back. I faxed over to him the necessary documents for him to ‚Äútake a look at‚Äù. From there after 5 days of no response, I decided to track him down. He says ‚Äúhe was busy but needed more information‚Äù. So I faxed him again more documents‚Ä¶ waited 5 more days of non response. Again I had to proactively track him down. This time he mentions, ‚ÄúIt was his fault and he filed the taxes incorrectly but I would still have to pay the $8,885 to the IRS. Because I didn‚Äôt get the ‚ÄúPeace of Mind‚Äù Insurance Guarantee that H&R Block Offers‚Äù.

I don‚Äôt understand why I would have to spend extra money for ‚ÄúPeace of Mind‚Äù when these are professionals whom I initially went to for, Peace of Mind.

In the end, Fred Stevens said he will ‚Äútry to make a claim‚Äù for me, but ultimately I don‚Äôt believe in his lies. Their website may say that Fred has 35+ Years of experience on there, but his professionalism is far from ideal. A true professional should be proactive in helping his clients. I feel that Fred is trying to avoid his mistakes. I have no faith in this company, nor would I ever have any faith in Fred.

Update.. it‚Äôs been day 3 since I last spoke to Fred and still no response or call back from him.

<time>1527185797787< /time><rating>5< /rating>< Review>
As the buyer's agent, we had a sewer inspection done on an almost totally rebuilt home (torn down to studs and remodeled).  We were not expected to have any sewer problems since the pipes had been changed also. We were surprised that the inspection report showed a section of the sewer pipe was disconnected and forming a valley which is likely to cause clogs in the future. We requested the Seller to repair. Seller agreed. His contractor repaired. But when we did the re-inspection, the inspector said "no change" from the previous one. Seller refused to do further repair. Buyer stayed firm wanting seller to repair, and we could not move forward. I was able to reach Rick Coffman quickly to asked him to explain why such a situation might arise (repaired, but problem not really fixed).  He explained to me with such clarity that I could understand, and he suggested a way for us to move forward to get a third-party consultation. I gave his contact info to the listing agent and his seller, and it looks like we will get it resolved soon. This was a good learning experience for me as well, and once the problem is resolved, both seller and buyer will be happy!< /Review>

<Text>After enjoying many tasty meals in the past year at the Holy Spirit Saturday brunch, I've been trying to make it back after a couple of months of missing out. So I was happy to find my way onto the 99 AC Transit bus that stops close to the church cafeteria and the sound of bells let  me know it was only 10 am. <Text>I am amazed at how well this church is run.  Everything they do is extremely well thought out and I have never been to another church that had this level of... thoughtfulness in everything the deliver during the mass.  High def projectors, higher end sound system, HD TVs and other technologies are integrated into the presentation in an unobtrusive and balanced way.  The crowd is also one of the most diverse I have seen with other parishes having a heavier lean towards a specific ethnic group, this one seems to carry a good mix of white, black, Asian and Indian.  The beginning of the mass always opens with welcoming visitors, and transitions into special sessions during mass for children in different age groups where they are led away in groups to get attention for the early part of the mass and return part way through.  In many ways, I feel the spirit and quality of the presentation here should be a model for other parishes but I recognize the uniqueness and culture that others may have on their own.  This one just resonates very well with me.<//Text><response>None</response></record></dataset><record>

< Text>
I was in town during Lent / Easter, and went to this Catholic Church.  It's very old, and very beautiful.  Built by the Portuguese immigrants and now heavily Philipino.  The priests are very, very friendly - especially Father Matt.

They have the usual mass services, but a lively community of supportive and wonderful folk.

Worth a visit if you are in town, or new to town and a Catholic.< /Text>

Fun place to play indoor soccer. The staff is really friendly and the refs overall are pretty good. Just like anything there are some really bad calls but for the most part they control the games so it doesnt get out of hand with the fouls. Personally i find it a little expensive to play here but I also havent played in Los Angeles anywhere else. San Diego leagues were quite a bit cheaper but i have been told this is about the norm for up here. The fields could use some new turf in front of the goal areas as the oatches are not done very well and have a decent lip to them. As a goalie I notice it a lot when moving back and forth across the goal. Other than that its a good place to play and the players dont play cheap and try to injure you.</review>

<date>1462746890903</date><rate>3</rate><review>Absolutely fine, nothing to write home about.

I found most of the food to be very one-dimensional, lacking the depth of flavor that takes food from okay to great. I had a caesar salad that lacked any rich, meaty anchovy flavor. The salad was small, despite being the "regular" size between small and large. I also had the pescatore, spaghetti with calamari, scallops, mussels, and shrimp. The sauce could have used more flavor, be it garlic, pepper, or literally anything. It was quite thin and tasted solely of tomato. The spaghetti was cooked perfectly al dente, however, and the scallops were not a second overcooked. The shrimp was well flavored - I wish some of that had translated to the rest of the dish! The pasta could have used more seafood as well. While the mussels were plentiful, the shrimp, calamari, and scallop felt a bit stingy.

Overall, nothing special. It wasn't bad, but I'm not sure I'd come back with so many great places to eat in Wine Country.</review>< Pics>
